google_ad_request_done(google_ads)
{




window['google_ads']
=
google_ads;




if(google_ads.length
!=
0)
{








apply_ad_config(google_ads.length);









render_ads(true,
window['ad_config_top']);









if(window['backfillParam'])
{












window['backfillParam']['pl_rnum']
=
google_ads.length;












window['backfillParam']['pl_time']
=
Date.now()
-
afc_ad_start_time;








}




}
}

function
apply_ad_config(num)
{
window['ad_config_top']
=
Math.min(2,
num);
window['ad_config_bot']
=
Math.min(2,
num);
}

google_ad_client
=
'ca-aj-cat';
google_ad_channel
=
'cx_ask_wiki,ad_dirN';
google_ad_output
=
'js';
google_max_num_ads
=
'4';
google_ad_type
=
'text';
google_image_size
=
'';
google_num_ads_recieved=
'';
google_language
=
'';
google_country
=
'';
google_encoding
=
'utf8';
google_safe
=
'medium';
google_adtest
=
'off';
google_ad_section
=
'default';
google_page_url
=
'';
google_hints
=
'Carrie_Underwood';
google_kw
=
'';
google_kw_type
=
'broad';


var
backfillParam
=
{




pl_rqnum
:
google_max_num_ads,




pl_hints
:
google_hints,




pl_rp
:
"false",




pl_kw
:
google_kw,




pl_cl
:
google_ad_client,




pl_ch
:
google_ad_channel,




pl_hex
:
"#FDFEEE",




pl_type
:
"afc",




pl_clksp
:
"none"};

var
word_arr
;

var
word_arr_len
;


function
highlightQuery(input_str)
{

var
queryTokenArray
=
"underwood,_,carrie,";


var
tok_arr
=
queryTokenArray.split(",");

for(tok_arr_idx=0;
tok_arr_idx
<
tok_arr.length-1;
tok_arr_idx
++)
{

if(isCombinationWord(tok_arr[tok_arr_idx])){
word_arr
=
tok_arr[tok_arr_idx].split("-");
word_arr_len
=
word_arr.length;
first_pos
=
input_str.toLowerCase().indexOf(word_arr[0],0);

if(first_pos
!=-1)
{
input_str
=
highlightCombinationWords(input_str,first_pos);
}
}
else
{
first_pos
=
input_str.toLowerCase().indexOf(tok_arr[tok_arr_idx],0);
if(first_pos
!=
-1
&&
tok_arr[tok_arr_idx].length
>
0)
{
input_str
=
highlightSimpleWords(input_str,tok_arr[tok_arr_idx],first_pos);
}
}
}
return
input_str;
}

function
isCombinationWord(word){
if(word.indexOf("-")
!=
-1){
return
true;
}
else
{
return
false;
}
}


function
isAlpha(ch)
{
if
(ch
!=
null
&&
ch.match(/^[a-zA-Z0-9]+$/)){
return
true;
}
return
false;
}

function
isQueryinInput(firstindex,
input_str,
j){
for(i=firstindex;
i<
input_str.length
;
++i)
{
var
currindex
=
i;

if(!isAlpha(input_str.charAt(i)))
{
if(firstindex
==
currindex)

{
firstindex++;
}
else
{
if(word_arr[j]
!=
input_str.substring(firstindex,currindex).toLowerCase())
return
-1;
if
(j
==
word_arr_len-1)
return
currindex;
else
return
isQueryinInput(currindex+1,input_str,++j);
}
}
}

if(j
<
word_arr_len)
{
if(word_arr[j]
!=
input_str.substring(firstindex,currindex+1).toLowerCase())
return
-1;
}

return
(currindex
+
1)
;
}


function

highlightCombinationWords(input_str,first_pos)
{
exactmatch
=
isQueryinInput(first_pos+word_arr[0].length,input_str,1)
;
if(exactmatch
!=-1
)

{
bold_str
=
"<b>"
+
input_str.substring(first_pos,exactmatch)
+
"</b>";
input_str
=
input_str.substring(0,first_pos)
+
bold_str
+
input_str.substring(exactmatch);
next_pos
=
input_str.toLowerCase().indexOf(word_arr[0],exactmatch+7);
while(next_pos
!=
-1)
{
return
highlightCombinationWords(input_str,next_pos);
}
}
return
input_str;
}


function

highlightSimpleWords(input_str,token,
first_pos)
{
var
end_pos
=
first_pos
+
token.length;
if(!isAlpha(input_str.charAt(end_pos))
&&
!isAlpha(input_str.charAt(first_pos-1))){
bold_str
=
"<b>"
+
input_str.substring(first_pos,end_pos)
+
"</b>";
input_str
=
input_str.substring(0,first_pos)
+
bold_str
+
input_str.substring(end_pos);
next_pos
=
input_str.toLowerCase().indexOf(token,end_pos+7);
}
else
{
next_pos
=
input_str.toLowerCase().indexOf(token,end_pos);
}

while(next_pos
!=
-1)
{
return
highlightSimpleWords(input_str,token,next_pos);
}
return
input_str;
}</script>

<p><b>Carrie
Marie
Underwood</b>
(born
March
10,
1983)
is
an
American
<a
href="/wiki/Country_music?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Country
music">country
music</a>
singer,
songwriter,
and
actress.
She
rose
to
fame
as
the
winner
of
the
<a
href="/wiki/American_Idol_(season_4)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="American
Idol
(season
4)">fourth
season</a>
of
<i><a
href="/wiki/American_Idol?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="American
Idol">American
Idol</a></i>
in
2005.
Underwood
has
since
become
a
<a
href="/wiki/Music_recording_sales_certification?qsrc=3044#List_of_international_sales_certification_thresholds"
title="Music
recording
sales
certification">multi-platinum
selling</a>
recording
artist,
a
winner
of
six
<a
href="/wiki/Grammy_Award?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Grammy
Award">Grammy
Awards</a>,
sixteen
<a
href="/wiki/Billboard_Music_Awards?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Billboard
Music
Awards"
class="mw-redirect"><i>Billboard</i>
Music
Awards</a>,
seven
<a
href="/wiki/American_Music_Awards?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="American
Music
Awards"
class="mw-redirect">American
Music
Awards</a>
and
ten
<a
href="/wiki/Academy_of_Country_Music_Awards?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Academy
of
Country
Music
Awards">Academy
of
Country
Music
Awards</a>,
among
several
others.
As
a
songwriter,
she
has
been
nominated
for
a
<a
href="/wiki/Golden_Globe_Award_for_Best_Original_Song?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Golden
Globe
Award
for
Best
Original
Song">Golden
Globe
Award
for
Best
Original
Song</a>.
Underwood
is
also
a
two-time
winner
of
the
Academy
of
Country
Music
<i>Entertainer
of
the
Year</i>
award
and
the
first
woman
to
win
such
an
award
twice
(2009/10).
Underwood
was
inducted
into
and
became
a
member
of
the
<a
href="/wiki/Grand_Ole_Opry?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Grand
Ole
Opry">Grand
Ole
Opry</a>
in
2008.
She
was
also
inducted
into
the
<a
href="/wiki/Oklahoma_Music_Hall_of_Fame?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Oklahoma
Music
Hall
of
Fame">Oklahoma
Music
Hall
of
Fame</a>
in
2009.<sup
id="cite_ref-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Her
debut
album,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Some_Hearts_(Carrie_Underwood_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Some
Hearts
(Carrie
Underwood
album)">Some
Hearts</a></i>,
was
released
in
2005.
Bolstered
by
the
huge
<a
href="/wiki/Crossover_(music)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Crossover
(music)">crossover</a>
success
of
the
singles
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Before_He_Cheats?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Before
He
Cheats">Before
He
Cheats</a>&quot;
and
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Jesus,_Take_the_Wheel?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Jesus,
Take
the
Wheel">Jesus,
Take
the
Wheel</a>&quot;,
it
went
on
to
become
the
fastest
selling
debut
country
album
in
<a
href="/wiki/Nielsen_SoundScan?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Nielsen
SoundScan">Nielsen
SoundScan</a>
history,
the
best-selling
solo
female
debut
album
in
country
music
history
and
the
best-selling
country
album
of
the
last
ten
years.
Underwood
won
three
<a
href="/wiki/Grammy_Awards?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Grammy
Awards"
class="mw-redirect">Grammy
Awards</a>
for
the
album,
including
<a
href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_New_Artist?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Grammy
Award
for
Best
New
Artist">Best
New
Artist</a>.
Her
second
album,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Carnival_Ride?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Carnival
Ride">Carnival
Ride</a></i>,
was
released
in
2007,
with
one
of
the
biggest
opening
weeks
by
a
female
artist
in
history,
and
later
earned
Underwood
two
Grammy
Awards,
for
the
singles
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Last_Name?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Last
Name">Last
Name</a>&quot;
and
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/I_Told_You_So_(Randy_Travis_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="I
Told
You
So
(Randy
Travis
song)">I
Told
You
So</a>&quot;.
Released
in
2009,
her
third
album,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Play_On_(Carrie_Underwood_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Play
On
(Carrie
Underwood
album)">Play
On</a></i>,
was
led
by
the
success
of
its
first
single,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Cowboy_Casanova?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Cowboy
Casanova">Cowboy
Casanova</a>&quot;,
and
finished
the
year
as
the
second
top-selling
release
by
a
female
artist.
2012's
<i><a
href="/wiki/Blown_Away_(album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Blown
Away
(album)">Blown
Away</a></i>,
her
fourth
album,
was
ranked
the
second
best-selling
release
of
the
year
by
a
female
artist.
She
won
a
Grammy
Award
for
the
album's
song
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Blown_Away_(song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Blown
Away
(song)">Blown
Away</a>&quot;.
With
her
strong
album
and
single
sales,
and
$100
million
in
tour
revenues,
Underwood
is
the
biggest
<i>American
Idol</i>
earner,
the
highest-ranked
<i>American
Idol</i>
alumni
on
the
<a
href="/wiki/RIAA?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="RIAA"
class="mw-redirect">RIAA</a>'s
Top
Digital
Artists
of
all
time
list
and
the
fourth
biggest
album
seller
of
the
past
ten
years.
She
has
sold
more
than
30
million
singles
and
16
million
albums
worldwide.</p>








<p>Described
by
music
critics
as
<a
href="/wiki/Honorific_nicknames_in_popular_music?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Honorific
nicknames
in
popular
music">Country
Music's
reigning
Queen</a>,
Underwood
is
the
only
solo
country
artist
in
the
2000s
decade
to
have
a
number
one
hit
on
the
<a
href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Billboard
Hot
100"><i>Billboard</i>
Hot
100</a>
and
the
first
and
only
country
artist
to
ever
debut
at
number
one
on
the
Hot
100,
as
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Inside_Your_Heaven?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Inside
Your
Heaven">Inside
Your
Heaven</a>&quot;
topped
the
chart
in
2005.
She
is
also
the
female
country
artist
with
the
most
number
one
hits
on
the
<i>Billboard</i>
<a
href="/wiki/Hot_Country_Songs?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Hot
Country
Songs">Hot
Country
Songs</a>
chart,
from
1991
to
present,
having
12
number
one's
and
breaking
her
own
<i><a
href="/wiki/Guinness_Book_of_World_Records?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Guinness
Book
of
World
Records"
class="mw-redirect">Guinness
Book</a></i>
record
of
ten.
<i>Some
Hearts</i>
was
named
the
No.
1
Country
Album
of
the
2000
Decade
by
<i>Billboard</i>
and
she
was
the
top-ranked
female
artist
on
<i>Billboard</i>'s
Best
Country
Artists
of
the
2000
Decade
list.
<i><a
href="/wiki/Forbes?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Forbes">Forbes</a></i>
estimates
that
Underwood
is
worth
$100
million.</p>

style="overflow:hidden;height:;">

<h2><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Early_life">Early
life</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Carrie_Underwood&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1"
title="Edit
section:
Early
life">edit</a>]</span></h2>








<p>Underwood
was
born
to
Stephen
and
Carole
Underwood
on
March
10,
1983,
in
<a
href="/wiki/Muskogee,_Oklahoma?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Muskogee,
Oklahoma">Muskogee,
Oklahoma</a>.
She
was
raised
on
her
parents'
farm
in
the
rural
town
of
<a
href="/wiki/Checotah,_Oklahoma?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Checotah,
Oklahoma">Checotah,
Oklahoma</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-3"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup>
Her
father
worked
in
a
<a
href="/wiki/Sawmill?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Sawmill">sawmill</a>,
while
her
mother
taught
elementary
school.<sup
id="cite_ref-4"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup>
She
has
two
older
sisters,
Shanna
and
Stephanie.<sup
id="cite_ref-Biography_Today_5-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Biography_Today-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-6"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup>
During
her
childhood,
Underwood
performed
at
Robbins
Memorial
Talent
Show,
and
sang
at
her
local
church,
First
Free
Will
Baptist
Church.<sup
id="cite_ref-Biography_Today.2C_p.144_7-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Biography_Today.2C_p.144-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup>
She
later
sang
for
local
events
in
Checotah,
including
Old
Settler's
Day
and
the
<a
href="/wiki/Lion%27s_Club?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Lion's
Club"
class="mw-redirect">Lion's
Club</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-BuddyTV_8-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-BuddyTV-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>A
local
admirer
arranged
for
her
to
go
to
Nashville
when
she
was
14
to
audition
for
<a
href="/wiki/Capitol_Records?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Capitol
Records">Capitol
Records</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-Biography_Today.2C_p.144_7-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Biography_Today.2C_p.144-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
1996,
Capitol
Records
was
preparing
a
contract
for
Underwood
but
cancelled
it
when
company
management
changed.
Underwood
said
of
the
event,
&quot;I
honestly
think
it's
a
lot
better
that
nothing
came
out
of
it
now,
because
I
wouldn't
have
been
ready
then.
Everything
has
a
way
of
working
out.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-9"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup>
While
at
Checotah
High
School,
she
was
an
Honor
Society
member,
a
cheerleader,
and
played
basketball
and
softball.<sup
id="cite_ref-Biography_Today.2C_p.145_10-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Biography_Today.2C_p.145-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup>
Underwood
graduated
from
Checotah
High
School
in
2001
as
<a
href="/wiki/Salutatorian?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Salutatorian">salutatorian</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-BuddyTV_8-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-BuddyTV-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup>
She
chose
not
to
pursue
singing
after
graduation.
She
said,
&quot;After
high
school,
I
pretty
much
gave
up
on
the
dream
of
singing.
I
had
reached
a
point
in
my
life
where
I
had
to
be
practical
and
prepare
for
my
future
in
the
'real
world'&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-Biography_Today.2C_p.145_10-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Biography_Today.2C_p.145-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup>
She
attended
<a
href="/wiki/Northeastern_State_University?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Northeastern
State
University">Northeastern
State
University</a>
in
<a
href="/wiki/Tahlequah,_Oklahoma?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Tahlequah,
Oklahoma">Tahlequah,
Oklahoma</a>,
graduating
<i><a
href="/wiki/Latin_honors?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Latin
honors">magna
cum
laude</a></i>
in
2006
with
a
bachelor's
degree
in
<a
href="/wiki/Mass_communication?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Mass
communication">mass
communication</a>
and
an
emphasis
in
journalism.<sup
id="cite_ref-usatoday_11-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-usatoday-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup>
She
spent
part
of
one
of
her
summers
as
a
page
for
Oklahoma
State
Representative
Bobby
Frame.<sup
id="cite_ref-12"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup>
She
also
waited
tables
at
a
pizzeria,
worked
at
a
zoo,
and
at
a
veterinary
clinic.<sup
id="cite_ref-Biography_Today.2C_p.145_10-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Biography_Today.2C_p.145-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup>
Underwood
is
an
alumna
of
the
Alpha
Iota
chapter
of
<a
href="/wiki/Sigma_Sigma_Sigma?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Sigma
Sigma
Sigma">Sigma
Sigma
Sigma</a>
sorority.<sup
id="cite_ref-sigma_13-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-sigma-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup>
For
two
years
during
the
summer,
she
performed
in
Northeastern
State
University's
Downtown
Country
show
in
Tahlequah.
She
also
competed
in
numerous
beauty
pageants
at
the
university
and
was
selected
as
Miss
NSU
runner-up
in
2004.<sup
id="cite_ref-pbs_14-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-pbs-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<h2><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Career">Career</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Carrie_Underwood&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2"
title="Edit
section:
Career">edit</a>]</span></h2>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="2004.E2.80.9305:_American_Idol">2004–05:
<i>American
Idol</i></span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Carrie_Underwood&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3"
title="Edit
section:
2004–05:
American
Idol">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<div
class="rellink
relarticle
mainarticle">








Main
article:









<a
href="/wiki/American_Idol_(season_4)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="American
Idol
(season
4)">American
Idol
(season
4)</a>







</div>








<p>In
the
summer
of
2004,
Underwood
auditioned
for
<i><a
href="/wiki/American_Idol?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="American
Idol">American
Idol</a></i>
in
<a
href="/wiki/St._Louis?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="St.
Louis">St.
Louis</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Missouri?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Missouri">Missouri</a>.
After
she
sang
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Could%27ve_Been?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Could've
Been">Could've
Been</a>&quot;
by
<a
href="/wiki/Tiffany_(American_singer)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Tiffany
(American
singer)">Tiffany</a>
on
the
top
12
girls
night,
judge
<a
href="/wiki/Simon_Cowell?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Simon
Cowell">Simon
Cowell</a>
commented
that
she
would
be
one
of
the
favorites
to
win
the
competition.<sup
id="cite_ref-15"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-16"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup>
During
the
top
11
finalists'
performance
on
the
March
22,
2005,
<i>Idol</i>
episode,
Underwood
sang
a
rendition
of
the
number
one
1980s
rock
hit
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Alone_(Heart_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Alone
(Heart
song)">Alone</a>&quot;,
made
famous
by
<a
href="/wiki/Heart_(band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Heart
(band)">Heart</a>,
and
Cowell
predicted
that
Underwood
would
not
only
win
the
competition,
but
she
would
also
outsell
all
previous
<i>Idol</i>
winners.<sup
id="cite_ref-foxnews_17-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-foxnews-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup>
One
of
the
show's
producers
later
said
she
dominated
the
voting,
winning
every
week
handily.<sup
id="cite_ref-18"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-19"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup>
She
gained
a
fan
base
known
as
&quot;Carrie's
Care
Bears&quot;
during
the
course
of
the
show.
During
the
final,
she
sang
with
<a
href="/wiki/Rascal_Flatts?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rascal
Flatts">Rascal
Flatts</a>
their
song
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Bless_the_Broken_Road?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Bless
the
Broken
Road">Bless
the
Broken
Road</a>&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-20"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup>
On
May
25,
2005,
Underwood
became
the
season
four
winner.
Her
winnings
included
a
recording
contract
worth
at
least
a
million
dollars,
use
of
a
private
jet
for
a
year,
and
a
<a
href="/wiki/Ford_Mustang?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Ford
Mustang">Ford
Mustang</a>
convertible.<sup
id="cite_ref-21"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<table
class="wikitable
collapsible
autocollapse"

margin:1em

<tr>











<td>Top

<td>&quot;<a

onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"

<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="2005.E2.80.9307:_Breakthrough_and_major_success_with_Some_Hearts">2005–07:
Breakthrough
and
major
success
with
<i>Some
Hearts</i></span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Carrie_Underwood&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4"
title="Edit
section:
2005–07:
Breakthrough
and
major
success
with
Some
Hearts">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<div
class="thumb
tleft">









<div
class="thumbinner"
style="width:222px;">









<a
href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:CroppedCarrieUnderwoodAtTheWorldArena.jpg"

class="image"><img

<div

<div

<a

Underwood
performing
at
the











<a
href="/wiki/World_Arena,_Colorado_Springs?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="World
Arena,
Colorado
Springs">World
Arena</a>
in
December
2006









</div>









</div>








</div>








<p>Underwood's
music
career
began
with
the
release
of
her
first
single,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Inside_Your_Heaven?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Inside
Your
Heaven">Inside
Your
Heaven</a>&quot;,
on
June
14,
2005.
The
song
debuted
at
number
one
on
the
<a
href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Billboard
Hot
100"><i>Billboard</i>
Hot
100</a>,
with
Underwood
becoming
only
the
third
artist
to
bow
in
the
top
slot
since
chart
policy
changed
in
1998.<sup
id="cite_ref-22"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup>
She
also
broke
<i>Billboard</i>
chart
history
as
the
first
country
music
artist
ever
to
debut
at
No.
1
on
the
Hot
100
and
the
song
became
the
first
song
from
a
country
artist
to
go
to
No.
1
on
the
Hot
100
since
country
group
<a
href="/wiki/Lonestar?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Lonestar">Lonestar</a>'s
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Amazed?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Amazed">Amazed</a>&quot;
did
so
in
2000.<sup
id="cite_ref-23"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup>
&quot;Inside
Your
Heaven&quot;
is
the
only
single
by
a
solo
country
artist
in
the
2000
decade
to
reach
number
one
on
the
<i>Billboard</i>
Hot
100
chart.<sup
id="cite_ref-24"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup>
It
also
debuted
at
number
one
on
the
<a
href="/wiki/Pop_100?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Pop
100"><i>Billboard</i>
Pop
100</a>
and
on
the
<a
href="/wiki/Canadian_Singles_Chart?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Canadian
Singles
Chart">Canadian
Singles
Chart</a>,
topping
it
for
seven
consecutive
weeks,
becoming
the
longest
running
single
of
2005
in
Canada.
It
sold
nearly
one
million
copies
and
was
certified
gold
by
the
RIAA
and
two
times
platinum
by
the
CRIA.<sup
id="cite_ref-riaa.com_25-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-riaa.com-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-cert_26-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-cert-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup>
Underwood's
debut
album,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Some_Hearts_(Carrie_Underwood_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Some
Hearts
(Carrie
Underwood
album)">Some
Hearts</a></i>,
was
released
on
November
15,
2005,
entering
the
<a
href="/wiki/Billboard_charts?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Billboard
charts"><i>Billboard</i>
charts</a>
with
315,000
copies
sold,
debuting
at
number
one
on
the
<a
href="/wiki/Top_Country_Albums?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Top
Country
Albums"
class="mw-redirect"><i>Billboard</i>
Top
Country
Albums</a>
and
at
number
two
on
the
<a
href="/wiki/Billboard_200?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Billboard
200"><i>Billboard</i>
200</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-27"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
large
first
week
sales
of
<i>Some
Hearts</i>
made
it
the
biggest
debut
of
any
country
artist
since
the
advent
of
the
<a
href="/wiki/SoundScan?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="SoundScan"
class="mw-redirect">SoundScan</a>
system
in
1991.<sup
id="cite_ref-28"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup>
<i>Some
Hearts</i>
became
the
best-selling
album
of
2006
in
all
genres
in
the
United
States.<sup
id="cite_ref-29"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
album
was
also
the
best-selling
country
album
of
both
2006
and
2007,
making
Underwood
the
first
female
artist
in
<i>Billboard</i>
history
to
earn
back-to-back
honors
for
Top
Country
Album.<sup
id="cite_ref-30"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup>
Additionally,
it
was
the
best-selling
female
country
album
of
2005,
2006
and
2007.<sup
id="cite_ref-31"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup>
<i>Some
Hearts</i>
has
since
been
certified
seven
times
Platinum
by
the
<a
href="/wiki/RIAA?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="RIAA"
class="mw-redirect">RIAA</a>,
and
is
the
fastest-selling
debut
country
album
in
the
history
of
the
<a
href="/wiki/SoundScan?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="SoundScan"
class="mw-redirect">SoundScan</a>
era,<sup
id="cite_ref-cmt20070110_32-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-cmt20070110-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-cst_33-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-cst-33"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup>
the
best-selling
solo
female
debut
album
in
country
music
history,<sup
id="cite_ref-34"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-34"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup>
the
best-selling
Country
album
of
the
last
10
years,<sup
id="cite_ref-35"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
the
best-selling
album
by
an
American
Idol
alumni
in
the
U.S.<sup
id="cite_ref-36"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
album's
second
single,<sup
id="cite_ref-bullatlanta1_37-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-bullatlanta1-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup>
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Jesus,_Take_the_Wheel?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Jesus,
Take
the
Wheel">Jesus,
Take
the
Wheel</a>&quot;
was
released
to
radio
in
October
and
later
peaked
at
number
one
on
the
<i><a
href="/wiki/Billboard_(magazine)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Billboard
(magazine)">Billboard</a></i>
Hot
Country
Songs,
topping
it
for
six
consecutive
weeks,
and
at
twenty
on
the
Hot
100.<sup
id="cite_ref-38"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
song
sold
over
two
million
copies
and
was
certified
2-time
Platinum
by
the
RIAA.<sup
id="cite_ref-RIAA_39-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-RIAA-39"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup>
Underwood's
third
single,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Some_Hearts_(song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Some
Hearts
(song)">Some
Hearts</a>&quot;,
was
also
released
in
October,
but
just
to
the
pop
radios.
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Don%27t_Forget_to_Remember_Me?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Don't
Forget
to
Remember
Me">Don't
Forget
to
Remember
Me</a>&quot;,
her
fourth
single,
also
proved
successful,
reaching
number
two
on
the
<i>Billboard</i>
Hot
Country
Songs
chart.
Later
that
autumn,
Underwood's
third
country
single,<sup
id="cite_ref-bullatlanta1_37-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-bullatlanta1-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup>
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Before_He_Cheats?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Before
He
Cheats">Before
He
Cheats</a>&quot;,
hit
number
one
on
<i>Billboard</i>'s
Hot
Country
Songs,
staying
there
for
5
consecutive
weeks.<sup
id="cite_ref-40"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-40"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
song
peaked
at
number
eight
on
the
<i>Billboard</i>
Hot
100,
achieving
the
slowest
climb
ever
to
the
top
10
of
the
<i>Billboard</i>
Hot
100,
breaking
the
record
that
was
previously
held
by
<a
href="/wiki/Creed_(band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Creed
(band)">Creed</a>
from
July
2000.<sup
id="cite_ref-41"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
February
2008,
when
it
was
certified
two-time
Platinum,
&quot;Before
He
Cheats&quot;
became
the
first
country
song
to
ever
be
certified
multi-platinum
by
the
RIAA.<sup
id="cite_ref-42"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-42"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup>
It
has
now
been
certified
4
times
Platinum,
selling
nearly
four
million
copies,
and
is
the
fourth
best-selling
country
digital
song
of
all
time.<sup
id="cite_ref-riaa.com_25-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-riaa.com-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-43"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-43"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup>
On
April
11,
2007,
Underwood
continued
her
streak
of
top
Country
singles
with
the
release
of
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Wasted_(Carrie_Underwood_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Wasted
(Carrie
Underwood
song)">Wasted</a>&quot;,
which
peaked
at
number
one
on
the
Hot
Country
Songs
Chart,
sold
nearly
one
million
copies
and
was
certified
Gold
by
the
RIAA.<sup
id="cite_ref-autogenerated1958_44-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-autogenerated1958-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
August
2008,
the
&quot;Jesus,
Take
the
Wheel&quot;
ringtone
was
reported
to
have
been
certified
Platinum,
making
Underwood
the
first
country
artist
ever
to
have
two
songs
hit
Platinum
Mastertone
status
together
with
&quot;Before
He
Cheats&quot;,
which
had
been
certified
earlier
in
2007.<sup
id="cite_ref-45"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup>
Underwood
started
her
first
headlined
tour,
<a
href="/wiki/Carrie_Underwood:_Live_2006?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Carrie
Underwood:
Live
2006">Carrie
Underwood:
Live
2006</a>,
with
dates
across
<a
href="/wiki/North_America?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="North
America">North
America</a>.</p>








<p>At

<p>Underwood's
second
album,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Carnival_Ride?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Carnival
Ride">Carnival
Ride</a></i>,<sup
id="cite_ref-65"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-65"><span>[</span>65<span>]</span></a></sup>
was
released
in
October
2007.<sup
id="cite_ref-msnbc01_66-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-msnbc01-66"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup>
On
<i>Carnival
Ride</i>,
Underwood
was
more
involved
in
the
songwriting
process;
she
set
up
a
writers'
retreat
at
Nashville's
famed
<a
href="/wiki/Ryman_Auditorium?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Ryman
Auditorium">Ryman
Auditorium</a>
to
collaborate
with
such
Music
Row
tunesmiths
as
<a
href="/wiki/Hillary_Lindsey?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Hillary
Lindsey">Hillary
Lindsey</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Craig_Wiseman?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Craig
Wiseman">Craig
Wiseman</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Rivers_Rutherford?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rivers
Rutherford">Rivers
Rutherford</a>,
and
<a

onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"

Sampson">Gordie
Sampson</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-67"
class="reference"><a

<i>Carnival
Ride</i>
moved
over
527,000
copies
in
its
first
week,
debuting
at
number
one
on
both
the
<a
href="/wiki/Billboard_200?qsrc=3044"

title="Billboard
200"><i>Billboard</i>
200</a>
and
Top
Country
Albums,
as
well

on

<a
href="/wiki/Canadian_Albums_Chart?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Canadian
Albums
Chart">Canadian
Albums
Chart</a>,
one
of
the
biggest
first-week
sales
by
a
female
artist.<sup
id="cite_ref-68"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-68"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup>
<i>Carnival
Ride</i>
was
certified
double
platinum
in
just
two
months
after
its
release,
in
December.<sup
id="cite_ref-69"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-69"><span>[</span>69<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
album
is
certified
3-time
Platinum
by
the
<a
href="/wiki/RIAA?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="RIAA"
class="mw-redirect">RIAA</a>,
for
sales
of
over
three
million.
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/So_Small?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="So
Small">So
Small</a>&quot;,
the

from

was

and
reached
number
one
on
<i><a
href="/wiki/Billboard_(magazine)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Billboard
(magazine)">Billboard</a></i>'s
Hot
Country
Songs,
topping
it
for
three
consecutive
weeks.<sup
id="cite_ref-cmt20070731_70-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-cmt20070731-70"><span>[</span>70<span>]</span></a></sup>
&quot;<a

onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="All-American
Girl
(song)">All-American
Girl</a>&quot;,

on

<i>Billboard</i>
Hot
Country
Songs.
The
next
single,
&quot;<a

title="Last

the

on

since
<a

title="Shania
Twain">Shania
Twain</a>
in
1998.
&quot;<a

(Carrie
Underwood

<i><a

(Shania

The

&quot;<a

for

more

class="reference"><a

In

<a

<p>At

5

Artist
of

Female

and

Country

recorded
it.<sup
id="cite_ref-93"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-93"><span>[</span>93<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
November
2008,
Underwood
recorded
a
virtual
and
posthumous
duet
with
<a
href="/wiki/Elvis_Presley?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Elvis
Presley">Elvis
Presley</a>,
on
his
classic
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/I%27ll_Be_Home_For_Christmas?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="I'll
Be
Home
For
Christmas"
class="mw-redirect">I'll
Be
Home
For
Christmas</a>&quot;,
for
his
2008
album
<i>Christmas
Duets</i>.
Elvis'
ex-wife,
<a
href="/wiki/Priscilla_Presley?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Priscilla
Presley">Priscilla
Presley</a>,
herself
asked
Underwood
to
do
the
duet:
&quot;Priscilla
wanted
me
to
do
'I'll
Be
Home
For
Christmas'&quot;,
she
says.
&quot;I
couldn't
say
'no'.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-94"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-94"><span>[</span>94<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
March
2009,
she
tracked
a
cover
of
<a
href="/wiki/M%C3%B6tley_Cr%C3%BCe?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="M&ouml;tley
Cr&uuml;e">M&ouml;tley
Cr&uuml;e</a>'s
ballad
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Home_Sweet_Home_(M%C3%B6tley_Cr%C3%BCe_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Home
Sweet
Home
(M&ouml;tley
Cr&uuml;e
song)">Home
Sweet
Home</a>&quot;
for
the
<i>American
Idol</i>
<a
href="/wiki/American_Idol_(season_8)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="American
Idol
(season
8)">season
eight</a>
farewell
theme.<sup
id="cite_ref-95"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-95"><span>[</span>95<span>]</span></a></sup>
Her
version
debuted
at
number
21
on
the
Hot
100
Songs.</p>

<p>Underwood
released
her
third
studio
album,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Play_On_(Carrie_Underwood_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Play
On
(Carrie
Underwood
album)">Play
On</a></i>,
on
November
3,
2009.<sup
id="cite_ref-96"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-96"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
album
debuted
atop
both
the
<i>Billboard</i>
200
and
Top
Country
Albums,
selling
over
318,000
copies
in
its
first
week,
and
became,
upon
its
release,
the
top-selling
release
of
the
year
by
a
female
artist,
but
was
later
overtaken
by
<a
href="/wiki/Susan_Boyle?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Susan
Boyle">Susan
Boyle</a>'s
<i><a
href="/wiki/I_Dreamed_a_Dream_(album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="I
Dreamed
a
Dream
(album)">I
Dreamed
a
Dream</a></i>
and
finished
the
year
as
the
number
two.<sup
id="cite_ref-97"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-97"><span>[</span>97<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-98"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-98"><span>[</span>98<span>]</span></a></sup>
Underwood
wrote
a
song
with
pop/R&amp;B
singer-songwriter
<a
href="/wiki/Ne-Yo?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Ne-Yo">Ne-Yo</a>
for
the
album,
the
song
however
did
not
make
the
album.<sup
id="cite_ref-99"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-99"><span>[</span>99<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
first
single
from
the
album,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Cowboy_Casanova?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Cowboy
Casanova">Cowboy
Casanova</a>&quot;,
co-written
by
Underwood,
<a
href="/wiki/Brett_James?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Brett
James">Brett
James</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Hip_hop_music?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Hip
hop
music">hip
hop</a>
producer
<a
href="/wiki/Mike_Elizondo?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Mike
Elizondo">Mike
Elizondo</a>,
was
released
in
September
2009.
It
was
a
huge
success,
jumping
from
No.
96
to
No.
11
on
the
<i>Billboard</i>
Hot
100
in
its
second
week,
one
of
the
<a
href="/wiki/List_of_Billboard_Hot_100_chart_achievements_and_milestones?qsrc=3044#Biggest_single-week_upward_movements"
title="List
of
Billboard
Hot
100
chart
achievements
and
milestones">biggest
single-week
upwards
on
the
chart</a>
of
all
time.<sup
id="cite_ref-100"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-100"><span>[</span>100<span>]</span></a></sup>
It
later
peaked
at
number
one
on
<i>Billboard'</i>s
<a
href="/wiki/Hot_Country_Songs?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Hot
Country
Songs">Hot
Country
Songs</a>
in
just
ten
weeks,
the
year's
fastest
chart-topper
by
a
country
female
and
the
fastest
No.
1
of
her
career,<sup
id="cite_ref-101"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-101"><span>[</span>101<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
has
sold
over
2
million
copies,
being
certified
2-time
Platinum
by
the
RIAA.
Second
single,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Temporary_Home?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Temporary
Home">Temporary
Home</a>&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-102"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-102"><span>[</span>102<span>]</span></a></sup>
hit
number
one
on
the
<i>Billboard</i>
Hot
Country
Songs
and
the
RIAA
certified
it
Gold.<sup
id="cite_ref-theboot.com_103-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-theboot.com-103"><span>[</span>103<span>]</span></a></sup>
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Undo_It?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Undo
It">Undo
It</a>&quot;,
Underwood's
third
single
from
&quot;Play
On&quot;,
was
released
to
radio
in
May.
It
was
later
certified
Platinum
by
the
RIAA
and
hit
number
one
on
the
Hot
Country
Songs
chart,
giving
Underwood
her
tenth
number
one
single
on
the
Hot
Country
Songs.<sup
id="cite_ref-104"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-104"><span>[</span>104<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
4th
single
from
<i>Play
On</i>,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Mama%27s_Song?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Mama's
Song">Mama's
Song</a>&quot;,
was
released
to
country
radio
in
September,
peaked
at
two
on
the
Hot
Country
Songs
and
was
certified
Gold
by
the
RIAA.
The
album
is
certified
Double
Platinum
by
the
RIAA.<sup
id="cite_ref-riaa.com-2_105-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-riaa.com-2-105"><span>[</span>105<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Underwood's
<a
href="/wiki/Play_On_Tour?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Play
On
Tour">Play
On
Tour</a>
started
its
first
leg
on
March
11,
2010
in
<a
href="/wiki/Reading,_Pennsylvania?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Reading,
Pennsylvania">Reading,
Pennsylvania</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-106"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-106"><span>[</span>106<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
second
leg
of
the
tour
started
on
September
25,
2010
in
<a
href="/wiki/Portland,_Oregon?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Portland,
Oregon">Portland,
Oregon</a>,
and
ended
January
1,
2011
in
<a
href="/wiki/Detroit,_Michigan?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Detroit,
Michigan"
class="mw-redirect">Detroit,
Michigan</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-107"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-107"><span>[</span>107<span>]</span></a></sup>
Underwood
sold
out
the
prestigious
<a
href="/wiki/Hollywood_Bowl?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Hollywood
Bowl">Hollywood
Bowl</a>
on
October
2,
2010.<sup
id="cite_ref-108"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-108"><span>[</span>108<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
December
2010,
Pollstar.com
ranked
the
Play
On
Tour
one
of
the
Top
50
tours
of
2010,
at
number
18
on
the
North
American
raking,
and
number
31
worldwide.
<i>Billboard</i>
also
ranked
Underwood's
tour
at
number
24
for
all
worldwide
tours
of
2010.
On
January
4,
2011,
official
statistics
revealed
that
Underwood
played
to
over
1
million
fans
throughout
the
tour,<sup
id="cite_ref-109"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-109"><span>[</span>109<span>]</span></a></sup>
resulting
in
her
being
named
again
as
the
top-ranked
female
country
touring
artist
of
the
year.<sup
id="cite_ref-110"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-110"><span>[</span>110<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>At
the
<a
href="/wiki/2009_CMA_Awards?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="2009
CMA
Awards"
class="mw-redirect">2009
CMA
Awards</a>,
she
received
two
nominations
and
co-hosted
the
ceremony
with
Brad
Paisley.<sup
id="cite_ref-111"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-111"><span>[</span>111<span>]</span></a></sup>
Underwood
was
nominated
for
six
Academy
of
Country
Music
Awards.
At
the
show,
Underwood
was
named
Entertainer
of
the
Year,
making
her
the
first
woman
in
history
to
win
this
award
twice.<sup
id="cite_ref-112"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-112"><span>[</span>112<span>]</span></a></sup>
Host
<a
href="/wiki/Reba_McEntire?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Reba
McEntire">Reba
McEntire</a>
presented
Underwood
with
the
&quot;ACM
Triple
Crown
Award&quot;
signifying
her
winning
Top
New
Artist,
Top
Female
Vocalist,
and
Entertainer
of
the
Year
during
her
career.
She
was
only
the
second
Female
to
win
the
coveted
&quot;Triple
Crown
Award&quot;,
the
first
being
<a
href="/wiki/Barbara_Mandrell?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Barbara
Mandrell">Barbara
Mandrell</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-113"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-113"><span>[</span>113<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-114"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-114"><span>[</span>114<span>]</span></a></sup>
At
the
<a
href="/wiki/CMT_Music_Awards?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="CMT
Music
Awards">CMT
Music
Awards</a>
Underwood
walked
away
with
Video
of
the
Year
for
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Cowboy_Casanova?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Cowboy
Casanova">Cowboy
Casanova</a>&quot;
and
also
won
CMT
Performance
of
the
Year
for
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Temporary_Home?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Temporary
Home">Temporary
Home</a>&quot;
from
CMT:
Invitation
Only
presents
Carrie
Underwood.<sup
id="cite_ref-115"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-115"><span>[</span>115<span>]</span></a></sup>
Underwood
won
two
international
awards
at
the
8th
French
Country
Music
Awards,
which
were
Best
Female
Vocalist
and
Video
of
the
Year,
for
&quot;Cowboy
Casanova&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-116"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-116"><span>[</span>116<span>]</span></a></sup>
At
the
2010
<a
href="/wiki/American_Music_Awards?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="American
Music
Awards"
class="mw-redirect">American

Awards</a>,
she
won
&quot;Favorite
Country
Album&quot;,
for
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Play_On_(Carrie_Underwood_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Play
On
(Carrie
Underwood
album)">Play
On</a>&quot;,
making
her
the
only
artist
in
the

Award

to

in

id="cite_ref-117"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-117"><span>[</span>117<span>]</span></a></sup>
She
co-hosted
the
2010
<a
href="/wiki/CMA_Awards?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="CMA
Awards"
class="mw-redirect">CMA
Awards</a>
with
Brad
Paisley
for
the
third
year
in
a
row.
Underwood
was
the
2010
<a
href="/wiki/American_Country_Awards?qsrc=3044"

title="American
Country
Awards">American

Artist

(<i>Play

(&quot;Cowboy

of
the

for
(&quot;Cowboy
Casanova&quot;)
and

Artist
of

id="cite_ref-118"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-118"><span>[</span>118<span>]</span></a></sup>
At

was

for
'Best

&quot;<a

Underwood
was

<a

special

on

3,

At

<a

both
her

&quot;Undo
It&quot;
and
<a
href="/wiki/Aerosmith?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"

&quot;<a

In

2011,

was
one

women
to

by

<a

of

at

<i>Girls'

was
recognized
for

and

female

to

win

id="cite_ref-122"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-122"><span>[</span>122<span>]</span></a></sup>
At
the

<a
href="/wiki/Vince_Gill?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Vince

Gill</a>

&quot;Jesus,

and

on
a

performance
of
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/How_Great_Thou_Art_(hymn)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="How
Great
Thou
Art
(hymn)"
class="mw-redirect">How

Thou
Art</a>&quot;.
The

of

turned
into
a
<a
href="/wiki/Viral_video?qsrc=3044"

title="Viral
video">viral

views
on
<a

onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="YouTube">YouTube</a>
within
two
days.<sup
id="cite_ref-123"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-123"><span>[</span>123<span>]</span></a></sup>

December
5,
2011,
Underwood
won
three
awards
at

2011
<a

Female

of

Year
for

<p>In

<p><i><a
href="/wiki/Blown_Away_(album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Blown
Away
(album)">Blown
Away</a></i>,<sup
id="cite_ref-146"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-146"><span>[</span>146<span>]</span></a></sup>
Underwood's
fourth
album,
was
released
on
May
1,
2012.<sup
id="cite_ref-147"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-147"><span>[</span>147<span>]</span></a></sup>
Underwood
has
said
that
this
album
features
songs
with
a
&quot;darker
storyline.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-148"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-148"><span>[</span>148<span>]</span></a></sup>
Blown
Away
debuted
at
number
one
on
the
<i>Billboard</i>
200,
the
Country
Albums
Chart
and
the
Digital
Albums
chart
in
the
United
States,
selling
more
than
267,000
in
its
first
week.<sup
id="cite_ref-149"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-149"><span>[</span>149<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
first
single,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Good_Girl_(Carrie_Underwood_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Good
Girl
(Carrie
Underwood
song)">Good
Girl</a>&quot;,
was
released
to
the
<a
href="/wiki/ITunes_Store?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="ITunes
Store">iTunes
Store</a>
on
February
23,
2012.
It
was
officially
released
to
Country
radio
on
February
27,
2012.<sup
id="cite_ref-150"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-150"><span>[</span>150<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-151"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-151"><span>[</span>151<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
music
video
for
&quot;Good
Girl&quot;
premiered
on
<i><a
href="/wiki/Entertainment_Tonight?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Entertainment
Tonight">Entertainment
Tonight</a></i>
and
on
<i><a
href="/wiki/VEVO?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="VEVO"
class="mw-redirect">VEVO</a></i>
on
March
12,
2012.<sup
id="cite_ref-152"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-152"><span>[</span>152<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
song
peaked
at
number
one
on
the
<i>Billboard</i>
Hot
Country
Songs
chart,
giving
Underwood
her
twelfth
number
one
on
the
chart,<sup
id="cite_ref-billboard.com_153-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-billboard.com-153"><span>[</span>153<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
was
certified
Platinum
by
the
<a
href="/wiki/RIAA?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="RIAA"
class="mw-redirect">RIAA</a>
and
has
sold
over
1.5
million
copies.<sup
id="cite_ref-carrieunderwoodofficial.com_154-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-carrieunderwoodofficial.com-154"><span>[</span>154<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
song
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Blown_Away_(song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Blown
Away
(song)">Blown
Away</a>&quot;
was
released
as
the
second
single
from
the
album
on
July
9,
2012.
It
was
a
massive
success,
selling
over
2
million
copies,
being
certified
Double
Platinum,
reaching
the
Top
20
of
the
<i>Billboard</i>
Hot
100,
the
number
one
spot
on
the
<a
href="/wiki/Country_Airplay?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Country
Airplay">Billboard
Country
Airplay</a>
and
the
Top
2
of
the
<a
href="/wiki/Hot_Country_Songs?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Hot
Country
Songs">Top
Country
Songs</a>,
where
it
became
Underwood's
16th
Top
10
hit
on
<i>Billboard'</i>s
Hot
Country
Songs,
a
record
among
women
in
the
tally’s
68-year
history.<sup
id="cite_ref-155"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-155"><span>[</span>155<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
album
has
been
certified
Platinum
by
the
RIAA
and
was
the
7th
best-selling
album
of
2012,
the
second
best-selling
country
album
of
the
year
and
the
second
best-selling
release
by
a
female
artist
in
2012.<sup
id="cite_ref-156"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-156"><span>[</span>156<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
album
has
sold
1.5
million
copies
in
the
United
States
alone.<sup
id="cite_ref-157"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-157"><span>[</span>157<span>]</span></a></sup>
On
August
2012,
it
was
announced
that
Underwood
would
have
her
very
own
<a
href="/wiki/VH1?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="VH1">VH1</a>
Unplugged
(called
&quot;VH1

Carrie
Underwood
Unplugged&quot;)

<a

class="mw-redirect">Behind

episodes.<sup

&quot;<a

id="cite_ref-riaa.com-2_105-1"

class="reference"><a

In

&quot;<a

<p>On

1,
2012,
Underwood
announced
her
international

<i><a

dates,
of

in

<a
href="/wiki/UK?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"

on

21,

<a

2.<sup

<p>Underwood
has
been
described
by
music
critics,
such
as
<i><a
href="/wiki/Billboard_(magazine)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"

(magazine)">Billboard</a></i>'s,

<a

<i>American
Idol</i>

16

most
number
one

on

chart,

12

<i><a

<p>On

&quot;<a

<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="2014-present:_Upcoming_fifth_studio_album_and_tour">2014-present:
Upcoming
fifth
studio
album
and
tour</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Carrie_Underwood&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8"
title="Edit
section:
2014-present:
Upcoming
fifth
studio
album
and
tour">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p>Underwood
confirmed
that
she
began
planning
a
new
album
in
August
2013
and
would
start
prep
work
sometime
in
2014.<sup
id="cite_ref-197"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-197"><span>[</span>197<span>]</span></a></sup>
Underwood
told
<i>Billboard</i>,
&quot;After
<i>The
Sound
of
Music</i>,
I
feel
like
I
can
really
buckle
down
and
start
working
on
the
next
album.&quot;
Underwood
also
stated
she
has
been
planning
another
tour,
which
might
me
toned
down
form
her
earlier
ones,
stating,
“I
haven’t
thought
about
it
much
because
I
don’t
know
what
the
next
album
is
going
to
sound
like,
but
I
like
just
standing
there
and
singing,
too.
I
may
take
a
different
approach,
a
more
simple
approach
on
the
next
one.
I
loved
the
energy
that
rock
concerts
had,”
Underwood
told
<i>Billboard</i>.<sup
id="cite_ref-198"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-198"><span>[</span>198<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<h2><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Acting_career">Acting
career</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Carrie_Underwood&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9"
title="Edit
section:
Acting
career">edit</a>]</span></h2>








<p>Underwood
appeared
on
<i><a
href="/wiki/How_I_Met_Your_Mother?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="How
I
Met
Your
Mother">How
I
Met
Your
Mother</a></i>
in
March
2010.
She
played
the
part
of
Tiffany,
a
medical
sales
rep
that
forms
a
relationship
with
Ted.<sup
id="cite_ref-199"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-199"><span>[</span>199<span>]</span></a></sup>
This
was
the
second
highest
rated
episode
for
season
five,
gaining
10.48
million
viewers.
Brian
Zoromski
of
IGN
gave
the
episode
8.5
out
of
10.
He
was
surprised
how
well
Underwood
performed
in
her
first
acting
role.<sup
id="cite_ref-Hooked_Review_200-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Hooked_Review-200"><span>[</span>200<span>]</span></a></sup>
A
few
months
earlier,
she
appeared
in
an
episode
of
the
<a
href="/wiki/Public_Broadcasting_Service?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Public
Broadcasting
Service"
class="mw-redirect">PBS</a>
<a
href="/wiki/Children%27s_television_series?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Children's
television
series">children's
television
series</a>
<i><a
href="/wiki/Sesame_Street?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Sesame
Street">Sesame
Street</a></i>,
performing
a
<a
href="/wiki/Voice-over?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Voice-over">voice-over</a>
as
&quot;Carrie
Underworm&quot;,
a
parodied
&quot;worm&quot;
character.<sup
id="cite_ref-201"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-201"><span>[</span>201<span>]</span></a></sup>
Underwood
made
her
film
debut
in
<i><a
href="/wiki/Soul_Surfer_(film)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Soul
Surfer
(film)">Soul
Surfer</a></i>
in
April
2011.
She
played
Sarah
Hill,
the
church
youth
leader
who
helped
<a
href="/wiki/Bethany_Hamilton?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Bethany
Hamilton">Bethany
Hamilton</a>
overcome
the
obstacles
she
faced
after
the
shark
attack.<sup
id="cite_ref-202"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-202"><span>[</span>202<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-Carrie_Underwood_Soul_Surfer_203-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Carrie_Underwood_Soul_Surfer-203"><span>[</span>203<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>It
was
announced
by
NBC
Entertainment
Chairman
Robert
Greenblatt
on
November
30,
2012
that
Underwood
would
star
in
the
coveted
role
of
Maria
von
Trapp
in
NBC’s
<a
href="/wiki/The_Sound_of_Music_Live!?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The

of
Music
Live!">live
broadcast</a>
of
<i>The
Sound
of
Music</i>,
based
on
the
<a
href="/wiki/The_Sound_of_Music?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The

of
Music">original
Broadway
musical</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-NBC_musical_204-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-NBC_musical-204"><span>[</span>204<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
three-hour
telecast
aired
on
December
5,
2013.<sup
id="cite_ref-205"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-205"><span>[</span>205<span>]</span></a></sup>
NBC
is
partnered
with
the
producing
team
of
Craig
Zadan
and
Neil
Meron.
&quot;To
have
a

Carrie
Underwood
perform
Maria
in
‘The
Sound
of
Music’
–
and
in
such
a
very
special

is
exciting
beyond

said
Ted
Chapin,
President,
Rodgers
&amp;
Hammerstein.
“Part
of
the

of
Rodgers
and
Hammerstein
is
how
their
work
has
adapted
itself
to
so
many
different

certain
the

Underwood
brings
to

will

into

the

id="cite_ref-206"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-206"><span>[</span>206<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<h2><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Personal_life">Personal
life</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Carrie_Underwood&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10"
title="Edit
section:
Personal
life">edit</a>]</span></h2>








<p>Underwood
is
a
practicing
<a
href="/wiki/Christian?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Christian">Christian</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-207"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-207"><span>[</span>207<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-208"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-208"><span>[</span>208<span>]</span></a></sup>
She
and
her
mother
are
fans
of
writer
<a
href="/wiki/Stephen_King?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Stephen
King">Stephen
King</a>.
His
1980s
best-selling
book-turned-to-movie
<i><a
href="/wiki/Christine_(novel)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Christine
(novel)">Christine</a></i>
inspired
the
video
for
her
single
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Two_Black_Cadillacs?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Two
Black
Cadillacs">Two
Black
Cadillacs</a>&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-209"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-209"><span>[</span>209<span>]</span></a></sup>
Underwood
is
a
fan
of
musical
drama
show
<i><a
href="/wiki/Nashville_(2012_TV_series)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Nashville
(2012
TV
series)">Nashville</a></i><sup
id="cite_ref-210"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-210"><span>[</span>210<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
horror-themed
TV
shows
<i><a
href="/wiki/The_Following?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Following">The
Following</a></i><sup
id="cite_ref-211"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-211"><span>[</span>211<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
<i><a
href="/wiki/The_Walking_Dead_(TV_series)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Walking
Dead
(TV
series)">The
Walking
Dead</a></i>,
having
stated,
in
an
interview
with
<a
href="/wiki/Marie_Claire?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Marie
Claire">Marie
Claire</a>,
that
she
would
like
to
play
a
zombie
on
<i>The
Walking
Dead</i>.<sup
id="cite_ref-212"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-212"><span>[</span>212<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<h3><span

<p>Underwood
began
dating
then
<a
href="/wiki/Ottawa_Senators?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Ottawa
Senators">Ottawa

(now
<a

<a

title="Ice
hockey">hockey</a>
player
<a

Fisher
(ice

Fisher</a>
after
they
met
at
one
of
her

in
late
2008
and
she
became
engaged
to
him
in
December
2009.<sup
id="cite_ref-213"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-213"><span>[</span>213<span>]</span></a></sup>
Underwood
and
Fisher
appeared
together
publicly
for
the
first
time
in
January
2010,
at
the
Bell
Sens
Soiree,
an
annual
fundraiser
in
<a
href="/wiki/Gatineau?qsrc=3044"

<a

onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Ottawa
Senators">Ottawa

id="cite_ref-214"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-214"><span>[</span>214<span>]</span></a></sup>
After

together

the
<a
href="/wiki/Country_Music_Television?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Country

Awards
in

Underwood

id="cite_ref-215"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-215"><span>[</span>215<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>On
July
10,
2010,
Underwood
and
Fisher
wed
at
The
Ritz-Carlton
Lodge,
Reynolds
Plantation
in
<a
href="/wiki/Greensboro,_Georgia?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Greensboro,
Georgia">Greensboro,
Georgia</a>,
with

250

in

The

gave
<i><a
href="/wiki/People_(magazine)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="People
(magazine)">People</a></i>
the
following

they

&quot;Mike
&amp;
Carrie
Fisher&quot;:
&quot;We

other
and
to

According
to
<i>People</i>,
<a
href="/wiki/Monique_Lhuillier?qsrc=3044"

id="cite_ref-216"

<a

<a

<p>On
February
11,
2011,
an
Ottawa
radio
station,
105.3
<a
href="/wiki/CISS-FM?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="CISS-FM">CISS-FM</a>,
banned
the
playing
of
Underwood's
music
because
her
husband,
Mike
Fisher,
was
traded
to
the
<a
href="/wiki/Nashville_Predators?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Nashville
Predators">Nashville
Predators</a>
the
day
before.
Due
to
Underwood's
fans'
threats
on
Facebook
to
never
tune
into
the
radio
station,
the
station
later
modified
their
statement.
They
apologized
for
their
actions,
saying
that
their
statements
were
meant
to
be
taken
as
a
joke,
as
they
do
not
play
Underwood's
country
songs
anyway
and
it
was
their
tongue-in-cheek
way
of
wishing
Fisher
the
best
of
luck
in
Nashville.<sup
id="cite_ref-221"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-221"><span>[</span>221<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-222"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-222"><span>[</span>222<span>]</span></a></sup>
Fisher
later
criticized
the
station
saying
&quot;obviously
Carrie
had
nothing
to
do
with
the
move
or
the
trade
or
anything
so
to
imply
something
like
that
was
just
wrong&quot;,
and
noting
that
both
he
and
Underwood
were
disappointed
in
the
negativity
that
was
created
by
the
radio
station.<sup
id="cite_ref-223"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-223"><span>[</span>223<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-224"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-224"><span>[</span>224<span>]</span></a></sup>
Underwood
was
selected
by
<i><a
href="/wiki/The_Hockey_News?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The

id="cite_ref-225"
class="reference"><a

<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Wealth">Wealth</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Carrie_Underwood&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12"
title="Edit
section:
Wealth">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p>According
to
<i><a
href="/wiki/Forbes?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Forbes">Forbes</a></i>,
Underwood
earned
$7
million
between
2006
and
2007,<sup
id="cite_ref-Forbes_63-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Forbes-63"><span>[</span>63<span>]</span></a></sup>
$9
million
between
2007
and
2008,<sup
id="cite_ref-forbes.com_90-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-forbes.com-90"><span>[</span>90<span>]</span></a></sup>
$14&nbsp;million
between
2008
and
2009,<sup
id="cite_ref-Top_Earning_Idols_91-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Top_Earning_Idols-91"><span>[</span>91<span>]</span></a></sup>
$13
million
between
2009
and
2010,<sup
id="cite_ref-http_140-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-http-140"><span>[</span>140<span>]</span></a></sup>
$20
million
between
2010
and
2011,<sup
id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_141-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-141"><span>[</span>141<span>]</span></a></sup>
$5
million
between
2011
and
2012
<sup
id="cite_ref-226"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-226"><span>[</span>226<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
$31
million
between
2012
and
2013<sup
id="cite_ref-The_2013_Celebrity_100_192-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-The_2013_Celebrity_100-192"><span>[</span>192<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-227"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-227"><span>[</span>227<span>]</span></a></sup>
Underwood's
total
net
worth
is
over
$100
million.</p>








<p>In
2010,
Underwood
and
Fisher
bought
a
mansion
on
11
acres
near
Ottawa,
Canada
in
the
luxurious
Spruce
Ridge.
Underwood
later
put
the
mansion
up
for
sale
at
an
asking
price
of
$2.2
million.<sup
id="cite_ref-Underwood_Mansion_228-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Underwood_Mansion-228"><span>[</span>228<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
2012,
Underwood
bought
a
cottage
outside
of
Tennessee.
Underwood
uses
this
cottage
for
weekend
get
aways.
Oprah
toured
and
interviewed
Underwood
and
Fisher
at
the
cottage
for
their
appearance
on
Oprah's
Next
Chapter.<sup
id="cite_ref-Underwood_Cottage_229-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Underwood_Cottage-229"><span>[</span>229<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In
January,
2014
it
was
reported
that
Underwood
topped
the
2013
list
of
the
highest-paid
American
Idol
alumni,
reportedly
earning
$31
million.
This
was
not
only

than

but
it
exceeded
the
annual
earnings
of
2013
judges
<a
href="/wiki/Mariah_Carey?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Mariah
Carey">Mariah
Carey</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Nicki_Minaj?qsrc=3044"

title="Nicki
Minaj">Nicki
Minaj</a>
and
<a

onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"

<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Personal_interests">Personal
interests</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Carrie_Underwood&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13"
title="Edit
section:
Personal
interests">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p>Underwood
is
an
animal
lover
and
a
<a
href="/wiki/Vegan?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Vegan"
class="mw-redirect">vegan</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-vegan_231-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-vegan-231"><span>[</span>231<span>]</span></a></sup>
She
stopped
eating
meat
at
the
age
of
thirteen
because
she
could
not
stand
the
thought
of
eating
one
of
her
own
animals.
She
was
voted
&quot;World's
Sexiest
Vegetarian&quot;
by
<a
href="/wiki/People_for_the_Ethical_Treatment_of_Animals?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="People
for
the
Ethical
Treatment
of
Animals">PETA</a><sup
id="cite_ref-goveg_232-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-goveg-232"><span>[</span>232<span>]</span></a></sup>
in
2007
for
the
second
time,
the
first
being
in
2005
alongside
<a
href="/wiki/Coldplay?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Coldplay">Coldplay</a>
frontman
<a
href="/wiki/Chris_Martin?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Chris
Martin">Chris
Martin</a>,
who
is
also
a
vegan.<sup
id="cite_ref-goveg_232-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-goveg-232"><span>[</span>232<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
a
2007
interview
with
PETA,
Underwood
stated,
&quot;Ever
since
I
was
little
I
loved
animals
[...]
If
you
told
me
I
could
never
sing
again,
I'd
say
that
was
horrible,
but
it's
not
my
life.
If
you
told
me
I
could
never
be
around
animals
again,
I
would
just
die.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-233"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-233"><span>[</span>233<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In
April
2013,
Underwood,
an
animal
lover,
spoke
out
with
disapproval
regarding
the
Tennessee
&quot;Ag
Gag
bill&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-234"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-234"><span>[</span>234<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
bill
makes
it
a
crime
to
videotape
animal
cruelty
or
abuse
and
then
fail
to
turn
in
the
evidence
to
authorities
within
48
hours.
This
is
to
stop
animal
rights
activists
from
accumulating
enough
documentation
to
prove
that
animal
cruelty
is
routine
in
big
agribusiness.<sup
id="cite_ref-235"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-235"><span>[</span>235<span>]</span></a></sup>
Underwood
tweeted,
&quot;Shame
on
TN
lawmakers
for
passing
the
Ag
Gag
bill.
If
Gov.
Bill
Haslam
signs
this,
he
needs
to
expect
me
at
his
front
door.
Who's
with
me?&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-236"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-236"><span>[</span>236<span>]</span></a></sup>
State
Rep.
Andy
Holt
responded
to
her
tweet,
saying,
&quot;I
would
say
that
Carrie
Underwood
will
stick
to
singing,
I'll
stick
to
lawmaking.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-237"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-237"><span>[</span>237<span>]</span></a></sup>
Underwood
later
responded
via
Twitter,
&quot;I
should
stick
to
singing?
Wow…sorry,
I’m
just
a
tax
paying
citizen
concerned
for
the
safety
of
my
family.
#NoAgGag&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-238"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-238"><span>[</span>238<span>]</span></a></sup>
She
also
tweeted
Tennessee
Gov.
Bill
Haslam,
saying
&quot;Please
don't
sign
the
Ag
Gag
bill.
Think
about
the
welfare
of
the
animals
as
well
as
the
consumers.
I'm
begging
you...&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-239"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-239"><span>[</span>239<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
